  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3817c619-2e19-4b0a-9e56-7b4b1e672a61'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer7973708639176561241">Kell is one of the last Antari—magicians with a rare, coveted ability to travel between parallel Londons; Red, Grey, White, and, once upon a time, Black.<br/><br/>Kell was raised in Arnes—Red London—and officially serves the Maresh Empire as an ambassador, traveling between the frequent bloody regime changes in White London and the court of George III in the dullest of Londons, the </span>
  <span id="freeText7973708639176561241" style="display:none">Kell is one of the last Antari—magicians with a rare, coveted ability to travel between parallel Londons; Red, Grey, White, and, once upon a time, Black.<br /><br />Kell was raised in Arnes—Red London—and officially serves the Maresh Empire as an ambassador, traveling between the frequent bloody regime changes in White London and the court of George III in the dullest of Londons, the one without any magic left to see.<br /><br />Unofficially, Kell is a smuggler, servicing people willing to pay for even the smallest glimpses of a world they'll never see. It's a defiant hobby with dangerous consequences, which Kell is now seeing firsthand.<br /><br />After an exchange goes awry, Kell escapes to Grey London and runs into Delilah Bard, a cut-purse with lofty aspirations. She first robs him, then saves him from a deadly enemy, and finally forces Kell to spirit her to another world for a proper adventure.<br /><br />Now perilous magic is afoot, and treachery lurks at every turn. To save all of the worlds, they'll first need to stay alive.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7973708639176561241" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div id="review_882260191" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/882260191" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/882260191?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer882260191" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3169219542899856903"><i>
  <blockquote>Every night of the year, the market lived and breathed and thrived. The stalls were always changing, but the energy remained, as much a part of the city as the river it fed on. Kell traced the edge of the bank, weaving through the evening fair, savoring the taste and smell of the air, the sound of laughter and music, the thrum of magic.</blockquote>
</i><br/>I'm already a Victoria Schwab fan after reading her good vs evil superhero urban fantasy novel - <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13638125.Vicious__Vicious___1_' title='Vicious (Vicious, #1) by V.E. Schwab' rel='nofollow noopener'>Vicious</a> - so I couldn't wait to get reacquainted with her add</span>
  <span id="freeText3169219542899856903" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>Every night of the year, the market lived and breathed and thrived. The stalls were always changing, but the energy remained, as much a part of the city as the river it fed on. Kell traced the edge of the bank, weaving through the evening fair, savoring the taste and smell of the air, the sound of laughter and music, the thrum of magic.</blockquote>
</i><br />I'm already a Victoria Schwab fan after reading her good vs evil superhero urban fantasy novel - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13638125.Vicious__Vicious___1_" title="Vicious (Vicious, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Vicious</a> - so I couldn't wait to get reacquainted with her addictive writing style, complex characters and wonderfully-conceived fantasy worlds. As it turns out, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22055262.A_Darker_Shade_of_Magic__Shades_of_Magic___1_" title="A Darker Shade of Magic (Shades of Magic, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">A Darker Shade of Magic</a> was even more than I'd expected.<br /><br />This book feels more like traditional fantasy than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13638125.Vicious__Vicious___1_" title="Vicious (Vicious, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Vicious</a> with the style, the invention of a new language, the large cast of characters, the magic, and the focus on royal/political dynamics. And yet, to use the word "traditional" anywhere near this novel is an injustice because <b>it's unlike anything I've ever read before.</b><br /><br />The characters are weird and colorful. We have a protagonist - Kell - who is strong and badass enough to root for, but also complex and layered enough for us to truly care about and relate to. Plus, he has a coat that has many sides, which he turns around depending on how he wants to look - insane, unique, wonderful. Schwab's imagination clearly knows no bounds.<br /><br />We also have a cross-dressing pirate who happens to be a tough, infuriating and lovable female character - Lila. And a promiscuous prince, villains who are blood slaves, evil twin rulers and much more. <br /><br />And then there's this bizarre world that just played on every one of my senses. The author asks us to believe in a setting that is incredibly farfetched and yet she breathes life into this world with evocative language and makes the unbelievable something we can picture in our heads. She shares little stories from this world's history to flesh out the picture:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>The infamous Krös Mejkt, the “Stone Forest,” was made up not of trees but of statues, all of them people. It was rumored the figures hadn’t always been stone, that the forest was actually a graveyard, kept by the Danes to commemorate those they killed, and remind any who passed through the outer wall of what happened to traitors in the twins’ London.</i>
</blockquote><br />What's all this about the "twins' London"? Well, in this world there are four different versions of London that only the Antari like Kell can move between. Technically, there are only three these days because Black London fell, consumed by its own misuse of magic. The others are Grey London (the one we know), Red London (the one Kell is from) and White London (ruled over by the sadistic Danes twins).<br /><br />Everyone, it seems, is out to use magic for their own selfish goals in this book. And when a mysterious relic from Black London - a relic that should have been destroyed - reappears, Kell and Lila must do what they can to protect it from all those who wish to claim it as their own.<br /><br /><b>Nothing short of a wild, fast-paced adventure.</b><br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/bookgeekreviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3169219542899856903" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1222038367" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1222038367" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1222038367?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mature-ya">mature-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=dark">dark</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1222038367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12449931482333194304"><b>
  <i>“I’d rather die on an adventure than live standing still.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>Isn’t it astonishing how upon our second readings of our favourite books, we discover so much more about our beloved characters and the world-building itself than the first time around?<br/><br/>And so in consequence to my rereading of <em>A Darker Shade of Magic</em> in order to be fully prepared (memory-wise) for <em>A Gathering of Shadows</em>, I started seeing redeemable qualities in Delilah Bard, the fierce, courageous (yet reckless) thief.<br/><br/>When she and Kell</span>
  <span id="freeText12449931482333194304" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“I’d rather die on an adventure than live standing still.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Isn’t it astonishing how upon our second readings of our favourite books, we discover so much more about our beloved characters and the world-building itself than the first time around?<br /><br />And so in consequence to my rereading of <em>A Darker Shade of Magic</em> in order to be fully prepared (memory-wise) for <em>A Gathering of Shadows</em>, I started seeing redeemable qualities in Delilah Bard, the fierce, courageous (yet reckless) thief.<br /><br />When she and Kell—the gorgeous Kell, my sweetheart, Kell—had gotten <em>closer </em>on my first reading of this book, I damn straight wanted to chop her head off.<br /><br /><em>But now, </em>my wish is only to smother her a little bit in her sleep—just a little bit.<br /><br />Progress, right? Saves me a death sentence.<br /><br /><em>A Darker Shade of Magic </em>is such a colourful book. I say that because there is not <em>one </em>dull character or moment in the story. Even Holland—yes, the poker-faced Holland—released a feeling inside of me… curiosity.<br /><br />It’s a dangerous world—forgive me, <em>worlds—</em>Kell lives in. In Red London is by far the most agreeable place to live in, but <em>the other worlds</em> (or shall I say ''alternative Londons'')—Grey London, White London and (dead) Black London—are not as pleasant.<br /><br />But magic runs through his blood, for he has a great purpose: to travel through the Londons for diplomatic purposes and to keep peace… He’s somewhat of a guardian to those lands.<br /><br />Kell is incredible. It’s—and I mean it—impossible to dislike him. He’s understanding, temperate, calm, powerful and charming without even trying to be (he really isn’t), unlike his brother, Rhy, whom I love dearly but do not get to spend much time with (what’s with not including him in the adventure, Miss Schwab?)<br /><br />Miss Schwab is a very skilled writer. What’s funny is that even though this is a relatively dark fantasy novel for (debatably) mature teenagers, it strangely feels like a fairytale, or a cautionary tale, rather. It’s just so… memorable and… re-readable, like a classic.<br /><br />Love, love, love! To all fantasy readers who have yet to plunge into <em>A Darker Shade of Magic, </em>feel my wrath! (You need read it.)<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12449931482333194304" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1552709885" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1552709885" />
    <a title="Rick Riordan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan"><img alt="Rick Riordan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442449448p2/25375513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1552709885?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rick Riordan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rick Riordan" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan">Rick Riordan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1552709885" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer423988184189529732">YA/adult Fantasy. There isn't just one London. There are, in fact, four cities sharing that name and geographic location, each in a very different plane of existence. The novel takes place in the early 1800s, when magical travel between the different Londons has been severely restricted. Long ago, the place called Black London underwent a massive magical accident -- a sort of implosion during which the forces of magic consumed the humans who tried to wield it. Since then, the doors between the w</span>
  <span id="freeText423988184189529732" style="display:none">YA/adult Fantasy. There isn't just one London. There are, in fact, four cities sharing that name and geographic location, each in a very different plane of existence. The novel takes place in the early 1800s, when magical travel between the different Londons has been severely restricted. Long ago, the place called Black London underwent a massive magical accident -- a sort of implosion during which the forces of magic consumed the humans who tried to wield it. Since then, the doors between the worlds have been sealed. The only ones who can travel from world to world are the blood magicians known as Travellers. When we first meet the traveler Kell, he has arrived in Grey London (in our own un-magical world) to deliver a message from his own sovereigns of Red London to King George III and the Prince Regent. The existence of other Londons, we learn, is a closely guarded secret that only the rulers know. We follow Kell's travels from Grey London to his home, the magical Red London, to the sinister world of White London, ruled by a pair of despot siblings who make Vlad the Impaler look like a nice guy. At the same time, we meet a young thief of Grey London named Lila Bard, whose life becomes entwined with Kell's accidentally as they are both plunged into a plot to reawaken magic and tear down the walls between the worlds.<br /><br />Phew! Just describing the book makes it seem complicated, and it is an intricate world that V.E. Schwab has created, but it's not as confusing as it seems. I highly recommend checking it out if you like fantasy. The idea of four separate Londons is fascinating, and like all the best fantasies, this novel makes its system of magic seem absolutely plausible. Me -- I hope I never get stuck in White London. That place is YIKES. Having said that, I would definitely sign up for more adventures with Kell and Lila!</span>
  <a data-text-id="423988184189529732" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1234861422" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1234861422" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1234861422?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1234861422" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1649219459876950509"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“As Travars,” he said. Travel. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>And oh boy, I did travel. I was covered in smoke, I tasted metal, I smelled roses, I wore a bizarre coat and I dreamed under a pale sky. But unfortunately, <b>I did not feel</b>.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450025076ra/17369733.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22055262.A_Darker_Shade_of_Magic__Shades_of_Magic___1_' title='A Darker Shade of Magic (Shades of Magic, #1) by V.E. Schwab' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Darker Shade of Magic</a> had <b>great potential</b>. The world <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7168230.V_E__Schwab' title='V.E. Schwab' rel='nofollow noopener'>V.E. Schwab</a> created is <b>fascinating</b>, full of <b>magic and blood</b>. There is Kell, an Antari, a blood magician who can travel between parallel universes, and Lila, a street thief who wants to become a pirate and experience great adventure</span>
  <span id="freeText1649219459876950509" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“As Travars,” he said. Travel. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>And oh boy, I did travel. I was covered in smoke, I tasted metal, I smelled roses, I wore a bizarre coat and I dreamed under a pale sky. But unfortunately, <b>I did not feel</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450025076ra/17369733.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22055262.A_Darker_Shade_of_Magic__Shades_of_Magic___1_" title="A Darker Shade of Magic (Shades of Magic, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">A Darker Shade of Magic</a> had <b>great potential</b>. The world <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7168230.V_E__Schwab" title="V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">V.E. Schwab</a> created is <b>fascinating</b>, full of <b>magic and blood</b>. There is Kell, an Antari, a blood magician who can travel between parallel universes, and Lila, a street thief who wants to become a pirate and experience great adventures, and when their fates interwine, they are the only ones who can save all three Londons from the tainted magic that destroyed the forth. I mean, it sounds pretty amazing, doesn't it?<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I'd rather die on an adventure than live standing still.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I can't say that the execution failed me, because I was all too eager to read Kell and Lila's story, to turn the pages and fight and travel and discover the mysteries of the powerful obsidian stone and uncover conspiracies and secrets. <b>But in the end I was unsatisfied.</b> I expected something more and my expectations were not met because <b>I couldn't connect with the characters.</b> They were superficial and I was <b>detached</b>. I didn't care about their fates, I didn't find in them the depth I wanted and the pang of enthusiasm I usually feel when I start a new series. I was just a silent observer, witnessing their story unfold without finding the spark of magic that would make me an active participant and cheer for them, worry for them and eventually love them. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472490634ra/20199861.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Lila annoyed me a couple of times with her imprudence and her recklessness but there is no doubt she was a badass and strong female lead. I liked Kell a little more and I waited for the signs that I was falling for him, but they never came. I'm still intrigued about his magic and his past though and I'm curious about the way his relationship with Lila will develop.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Some people steal to stay alive, and some steal to feel alive. Simple as that.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>I can't help but shake the feeling that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7168230.V_E__Schwab" title="V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">V.E. Schwab</a> had raised her wand, ready to cast the spell that would bewitch me but the words never left her lips.</b> Her plotline was like Red London, vivid and full of possibilities. Her characters like White London, dangerous yet somehow pale and faded. And me, well, I'm Grey London, magicless in the surface but waiting for the magic I know it exists to ignite. I don't know how to rate a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22055262.A_Darker_Shade_of_Magic__Shades_of_Magic___1_" title="A Darker Shade of Magic (Shades of Magic, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">A Darker Shade of Magic</a>. Four stars are too much, three not enough, and I'll have to settle with <b>3.5 and a hope that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20764879.A_Gathering_of_Shadows__Shades_of_Magic___2_" title="A Gathering of Shadows (Shades of Magic, #2) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">A Gathering of Shadows</a> will actually be the one that will disperse the shadows the debut of this trilogy cast.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472490634ra/20199862.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="1649219459876950509" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1212310806" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1212310806" />
    <a title="Darth J " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18974711-darth-j"><img alt="Darth J " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456429148p2/18974711.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1212310806?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Darth J " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Darth J " href="/user/show/18974711-darth-j">Darth J </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18974711-darth-j?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18974711-darth-j?shelf=slow">slow</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1212310806" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15640633869959852176"><b>An Overhyped Shade of Mediocre</b><br/><br/>Before you jump down my throat, I didn’t <i>hate</i> this novel as much as I felt let down by it. Let me explain: it’s been hyped up everywhere and when that happens, expectations tend to run very high. Think back to when you were a kid and wanted something for your birthday so much and were so sure that you were going to get it; and even if you got plenty of nice things, the fact that you didn’t get the one thing you wanted made you disappointed. That’s the same feeling I</span>
  <span id="freeText15640633869959852176" style="display:none"><b>An Overhyped Shade of Mediocre</b><br><br>Before you jump down my throat, I didn’t <i>hate</i> this novel as much as I felt let down by it. Let me explain: it’s been hyped up everywhere and when that happens, expectations tend to run very high. Think back to when you were a kid and wanted something for your birthday so much and were so sure that you were going to get it; and even if you got plenty of nice things, the fact that you didn’t get the one thing you wanted made you disappointed. That’s the same feeling I got from this book.<br><br>Further, I felt like there was a lot of pandering going on here. Currently, YA books are trying their darnedest to be inclusive, which I personally think is a great step in modern storytelling. However, I don’t care for having one-dimensional characters just for the sake of faux-representation. Prince Rhy is well, a prince, but he’s also bi/pan/omnisexual…. and that’s about it. Sure he is our MC’s best friend/adopted brother and serves some purpose in the story, but he’s mostly a token character since there is nothing more to him. Our second case of pandering comes from our female MC, Lila*. She’s a tough female protagonist with a dark past, because <i>we’ve never seen that before.</i> *eye roll* Okay, I get that audiences need strong female characters and are sick of Mary Sues, but Lila reads like a stock character. She’s tepid and boring, just like the writing.<br><br>This book took me longer to finish than I would have thought, simply because the writing is so dry and flat. On nearly every page I pendulated from interested to bored and back again like a metronome. The story itself is captivating in parts, but the actual prose has no life. There's no heart in it at all, and you don't care about the characters so when they die it's no big deal. It sits there listless and says, <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427301416i/14259412._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Our main character is Kell, and he is <i>oh so original</i>. You guys, he’s “one of the last travelers—magicians with a rare, coveted ability”. Are there any protagonists that don’t have rare gifts anymore? Wait though, he has a completely black eye and does blood magic and there is only one other blood magician in the story so of course they have to face off. Not only that, the MacGuffin in this book is a stone split in half, and wouldn’t you know it? The other half of this stone belongs to the villain! I have never heard of a hero and villain having some sort of weird twin connection between their magical foci before /sarcasm<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427301416i/14259413.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Back to Lila. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I think it’s pretty clear that Lila is an Antari because she’s missing an eye (that probably would have been black like Kell’s) and there are strong hints that she has magic inside her, plus she can also travel worlds). <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It seems like the very idea of her was taken from watching Kiera Knightly in the <i>Pirates of the Caribbean </i> films. By the end, she has a pirate coat and is seen looking at a bunch of ships deciding which one to steal.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427301742ra/14259471.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There’s a lot to be confused about in this book too. Especially, trying to remember the differences between the 4 Londons. Yes, there are 4. It’s some alternate dimension thing?? There’s really no explanation as to why there are at least 4 different (overlapping) universes here other than the need for Kell to jump between them because of some quasi-political reasons.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427301742i/14259472.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>All in all, it’s interesting concept that was dryly executed with borrowed characters and buzz that will make you expect more than this book actually has to offer.</b> If you just want a mindless popcorn book made up of ideas seen elsewhere and are clueless enough to think that one-note tertiary characters are progressive, then you'll probably love it.<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="15640633869959852176" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_2370444128" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2370444128" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2370444128?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2370444128" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3036335548810198235"><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567353510i/28084553._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <br/>
  <br/>
  <i>“I'm not going to die," she said. "Not till I've seen it."<br/><br/>"Seen what?"<br/><br/>Her smile widened. "Everything.”</i>
</blockquote> Kell - one of the last Antari - is playing a dangerous game. Being an Antari, he <b>travels between worlds. </b><br/><br/>He knows of four worlds and all four of them have one, conveniently overlapping city:<b> London.</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>Grey London</i>
</b> - Magicless, technology driven.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>Red London</i>
</b> - Magic is considered a gift and is practiced with careful determination<br/><br/><b>
  <i>White London</i>
</b> - Magic is cruel, often needs to be</span>
  <span id="freeText3036335548810198235" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567353510i/28084553._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <br>
  <i>“I'm not going to die," she said. "Not till I've seen it."<br><br>"Seen what?"<br><br>Her smile widened. "Everything.”</i>
</blockquote> Kell - one of the last Antari - is playing a dangerous game. Being an Antari, he <b>travels between worlds. </b><br><br>He knows of four worlds and all four of them have one, conveniently overlapping city:<b> London.</b><br><br><b>
  <i>Grey London</i>
</b> - Magicless, technology driven.<br><br><b>
  <i>Red London</i>
</b> - Magic is considered a gift and is practiced with careful determination<br><br><b>
  <i>White London</i>
</b> - Magic is cruel, often needs to be stolen and locked into bodies<br><br><b>
  <i>Black London</i>
</b> - Magic is hungry and all-consuming, magic apocalypse happened here. All magic, artifacts and people from Black London is banned from the other worlds.<br><br>Kell frequently travels in and out of the Londons - passing along correspondence, adventuring and <b>smuggling artifacts</b> (that last bit is hugely illegal). <br><br>After a visit to the cruel king and queen of White London, Kell is given an <b>innocuous black stone </b>and told to bring it to Red London. A bit buzzed and confused, he travels between worlds only to discover that the stone is actually <b>a part of Black London.</b><br><br>By smuggling the stone, Kell <b>committed treason </b>against the crown of Red London (his adopted family) but more importantly, the black stone contains remnants of that world's magic - <b>seduction and hunger.</b><br><br>Delilah "Lila" Bard lives in Grey London (not that she knows it). It's the <b>only London without magic </b>and she's spent her entire life looking for a way out. And then Kell lands on her doorstop.<blockquote>
  <i>I'd rather die on an adventure than live standing still.</i>
</blockquote> Kell immediately struggles with the power of the stone. And he soon realizes that although he may not want it, <b>help will come to him </b> in the form of one very, very stubborn Lila Bard.<blockquote>
  <i>“Sure I do,” countered Lila cheerfully. “There’s Dull London, Kell London, Creepy London, and Dead London,” she recited, ticking them off on her fingers. “See? I’m a fast learner.” </i>
</blockquote>Whewww! I really enjoyed the start to this series!<br><br>Schwab had such a <b>unique idea </b>- with the four Londons and their varying degrees of magic - and executed it extremely well. I loved all the details she included - it really made the story come alive. <br><br>As for the characters...Lila (at times a bit over the top) really <b>balanced out the seriousness </b>and coldness of Kell. The two of them working together had a really natural feel - as evidenced by their <b>free-flowing banter.</b><blockquote>
  <i>“I apologize for anything I might have done. I was not myself.”<br><br>“I apologize for shooting you in the leg.” said Lila. “I was myself entirely.” </i>
</blockquote> I cannot wait to get started on book two!<br><br><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br>Read by Steven Crossley - and he did a great job. This was a rather well-read audiobook. I do wish he would've had more emotion when it came to his characters but then again, Kell is supposed to be a little stand-offish.<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3036335548810198235" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1139553606" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1139553606" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1139553606?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=best-of-2016">best-of-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1139553606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8261049793443560285"><b>
  <u>RE-READ UPDATE:</u>
</b><br/>So, in a startling turn of events, this book is even more insufferably perfect the second time round and I'm so in love with it I frequently forget WHAT AIR IS. I love Kell. I love his frown. I love his love for his brother. I love his smol fragile beginnings of a relationship with Lila. I love his bloody magic. I love his dark side.<br/><br/>I LOVE THIS BOOK AND THIS WORLD AND THESE CHARACTERS SO MUCH IT HURTS JUST A LTITLE WHICH CAN BE TRANSLATED A LOT.<br/><br/>Wow. I may need to go lie down o</span>
  <span id="freeText8261049793443560285" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>RE-READ UPDATE:</u>
</b><br />So, in a startling turn of events, this book is even more insufferably perfect the second time round and I'm so in love with it I frequently forget WHAT AIR IS. I love Kell. I love his frown. I love his love for his brother. I love his smol fragile beginnings of a relationship with Lila. I love his bloody magic. I love his dark side.<br /><br />I LOVE THIS BOOK AND THIS WORLD AND THESE CHARACTERS SO MUCH IT HURTS JUST A LTITLE WHICH CAN BE TRANSLATED A LOT.<br /><br />Wow. I may need to go lie down or else faceplant into <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20764879.A_Gathering_of_Shadows__Shades_of_Magic___2_" title="A Gathering of Shadows (Shades of Magic, #2) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">A Gathering of Shadows</a> for the second time. &lt;3<br /><br />(FYI the audiobook was fantastic.)<br /><br /><br /><b>ORIGINAL REVIEW: 2016:</b><br /><br />It took me 90001 years of procrastination to read this. I DOn'T EVEN KNOW WHY???? I over-hyped to <i>myself</i>??? (Despite already having read and adored <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13638125.Vicious__Vicious___1_" title="Vicious (Vicious, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Vicious</a>. So clearly I am the most pathetic of grapefruit fiends.) <b>So of course I ADORED this book.</b> It was violent and magicy and bloody and <i>incredibly written</i>...and I have a <b>severe love Kell's magical multi-sided coat.</b> Like seriously, I want one. YOU DON'T UNDERSTAND HOW MUCH I LOVE HIS FREAKING AWESOME COAT. Ahem.<br /><br />Also this book just had this WHOLE LIST of things I love...seriously, it's like it stole the checklist of "things Cait likes" and just completed it all perfectly. <br /><br /><b>For instance:</b><br />• Magical multi-sided coat ✓<br />• Characters who put things in pockets, like millions of things (I have a pocket infatuation btw) ✓<br />• Sassy, snarky witty banter ✓<br />• A girl who's #1 aspiration is to be a pirate (#goals) ✓<br />• Evil magic ✓<br />• Concise writing ✓<br />• Lots of stabby stabbing all the time ✓<br />• LIKE STABBY STAB EVERYTHING OMG ✓<br /><br />...I <i>told you</i>...IT WAS WRITTEN WITH ME IN MIND. (Ahem.)<br /><br /><b>Also I absolutely adore VE Schwab's writing style!!</b> Like it's brisk and too the point. It doesn't fluff around. And she is QUEEN of world-building. Gah, I am <i>in love</i> with the world building skills. Seriously not a lot of books manage to make a world this complex and dimensional but EASY TO UNDERSTAND so so simply and fast. I actually <b>never had any "Huh, I don't get it?" moments.</b> Which is a big deal for me. Because 87% of my life is spent saying "Wut. I don't get it." BUT NOT WHEN I READ A SCHWAB BOOK HUZZAH.<br /><br /><b>And the characters?! Omg...I shall pause here and SHRIEK MIGHTILY OF MY LOVE.</b> Shriek loudly, I tell you.<br /><br />• <b>Kell </b>was perfect. Like, literally <i>perfect</i>. A little bit tragic and lost and longing...and also totally sassy with the perfect comeback waiting. I love how basically the ENTIRE book is because he made a stupid mistake...so he's a gorgeous little darling, but at the same time immensely flawed.<br />• <b>Lila</b>, of course, is my hero. She's NASTY. She's a thief and so snarky...omg, she'd bite you. She really would. And she's <i>wondrous</i>. I love how she starts off just wanting an adventure -- BUT THEN SHE GETS A FRIEND IN KELL. &lt;333 And the way she and Kell continually had to save each other?!?!?? My favourite thing of ever.<br />•<b> Rhys</b> was definitely a potential favourite. I mean, I DID love him. He was really overconfident and dashing and dazzling and spoiled and vibrant and INCREDIBLE. My favourite kind of character, tbh....<i>but</i>....he really wasn't in the story very much. For this I am sad.<br />• <b>Holland?</b> I feel I want to mention Holland, who is another magician like Kell (they're the only two of their kind who can jump through worlds), and he was really CREEPY. But tragic? Like I felt really bad for him even as he was doing terrible evil things. He was enough of a villain to be hated, and enough of a victim to make me whisper a small "oh dear" and feel sad for him. #perfectwriting<br /><br /><br />...basically everything in this book was freaking perfect. nUNNNNNGH.<br /><br />OH WAIT. <b>One thing wasn't perfect.</b> But this is purely <i>me</i>? And I dare say most people wouldn't have this problem: <b>but I found the book very predictable. </b>Seriously I KNEW what plot twists were going to go down most of the time??? It was really weird. I have this slight suspicion that it's sort of how I would put together a story? (I am in NO WAY claiming to be as good of a writer as Schwab. HAHAHAH NOPE. I am like a toddler with a crayon compared to her. But...yeah. I would choose all the plot directions she went in, which made me sort of know they were going down?) SO THAT'S WEIRD. BUT THAT HAPPENED. <br /><br />Also pleeeeeeeeeeease tell me I'm not alone in catching the potential-plot-twist-about-Lila?!?!? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ LILA'S FREAKING MISSING EYE?!?! BAh. She is so totally an Antari. Clearly someone cut out her eye as a kid, right??? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />...also <b>I feel like I read somewhere that there was no romance in this book?</b> WELL HECK NO. I SHIP KELL AND LILA LIKE NOTHING ELSE. There was a kiss. That's ship material there.<br /><br /><b>I also really liked how it didn't spare the characters.</b> And like everyone's moral compasses were soooo twisted. AND THERE WAS TONS OF STABBING AND BLOOD EVERYWHERE. I'm like such a violent little squid. <i>I know</i>. But omg, so much blood. Everywhere. (Also it gives me the shivers when they cut themselves for spells. Ugh.)<br /><br /><b>So basically this book is perfect. BUT YOU ALREADY KNEW THAT.</b> And I'm actually glad I only read it just now?? Because I can go buy <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20764879.A_Gathering_of_Shadows__Shades_of_Magic___2_" title="A Gathering of Shadows (Shades of Magic, #2) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">A Gathering of Shadows</a> straight away! HAPPY DANCE. I love the characters, I <i>am so sucked in by the writing,</i> and I can't get enough of the epic dialogue and the perfect plot twists and the bloody spectacular brilliantness.<br /><br />YES I'M DONE GUSHING. OMG.<br /><br />(You can all say "I told you so" but I will smush cake in your face and glare.)<br /><br />(Also the part where Lila knocks Kell out with a book is basically the best part of the entire book and gives me life quite frankly.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="8261049793443560285" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2050203917" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2050203917" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2050203917?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/23403402-a-darker-shade-of-magic">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=fantasy-series">fantasy-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2050203917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17793063898984120000"><i>”Magic was a truly beautiful disease.”</i><br/><br/>And it was such a pleasure to read about it! XD I can’t say how much I loved and adored this book! Alone the magic in this was everything and it was so dark and twisted that it was a delight to read about it. In <b>“A Darker Shade of Magic”</b> magic is a living and breathing thing and it can help and heal at least as much as it can corrupt and destroy. In my opinion this was a really great concept and I lived and breathed for the execution of it. <br/><br/><i>”The words themse</i></span>
  <span id="freeText17793063898984120000" style="display:none"><i>”Magic was a truly beautiful disease.”</i><br /><br />And it was such a pleasure to read about it! XD I can’t say how much I loved and adored this book! Alone the magic in this was everything and it was so dark and twisted that it was a delight to read about it. In <b>“A Darker Shade of Magic”</b> magic is a living and breathing thing and it can help and heal at least as much as it can corrupt and destroy. In my opinion this was a really great concept and I lived and breathed for the execution of it. <br /><br /><i>”The words themselves were less important than the focus they brought to the speaker’s mind, the connection they helped to form, the power they tapped into. In short, the language did not matter, only the intention did.”</i><br /><br />Still, it wasn’t only the magical aspect of this book that kept me glued to the pages. The mere idea of four different parallel Londons that exist next to each other was more than just intriguing as well. Sure, we didn’t get to see an awful lot of them because the characters travel through them and don’t stay all too long, the little I saw was enough to keep me hooked though. ;-) London is my favourite city and the mere idea to explore four different versions of this town already made me feel like I won the jackpot. *lol*<br /><br />And last but not least “A Darker Shade of Magic” had its fair share of intriguing and complex characters that caused my eyes to sparkle. We all know that I can’t resist the temptation of morally grey and ambivalent characters so it’s no surprise that I savoured this like a delicious gourmet dinner. Alone the villains of this book!!! The Dane Twins were such evil creatures yet I couldn’t help but want to read more about them. Ohh and Holland! Don’t even get me started on Holland! &lt;3 Or well, maybe I actually should start to talk about him. In the characters section, of course! ;-P<br /><br /><b>The characters:</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Good afternoon, fellow Antari! It’s a good day to travel between the worlds but be careful nevertheless. There is always a shadow lurking at the next corner of the street and if you’re not cautious it will not only attack you but also spoil you big time as well! Tread carefully, my dear friend! You’re being observed by dark forces. ;-)</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>Kell:</b><br /><br /><i>”Kell tipped his head so that his copper hair tumbled out of his eyes, revealing not only the crisp blue of the left one but the solid black of the right. A black that ran edge to edge, filling white and iris both. There was nothing human about that eye. It was pure magic. The mark of a blood magician. Of an Antari.”</i><br /><br />I’m such a sucker for red-heads and Kell is really yummy. ;-P I can’t help it! Really! They are my kryptonite. Ask Lucien. *lol* Anyway, Kell is a really interesting character and he definitely has more depth than initially meets the eye. On the outside you might think that he’s the typical hero, but the more I discovered about his life, the more I felt sorry for him. He is part of the royal family and might seem to have it all, but when push came to shove his true status among the royals was revealed and my heart ached for him. I know Lila didn’t understand what he meant but by the end of the book it became pretty clear that he wasn’t really a family member but rather a valuable asset. At least when it came to his “parents”. Despite this he still had his own moral code and acted according to it, even if it meant that he was at a disadvantage when he had to face Holland and the Dane twins. Poor Kell! I had the feeling in some way or another he was figuratively and quite literally bleeding throughout the entire book. *lol* Let’s hope things will get better for him in “A Gathering of Shadows”! ;-)<br /><br /><i>”Magic was a living thing – that, everyone knew – but to Kell it felt like more, like a friend, like family. It was, after all, a part of him (much more than it was a part of most) and he couldn’t help feeling like it knew what he was saying, what he was feeling, not only when he summoned it, but always, in every heartbeat and every breath.”</i><br /><br /><i>She always went looking for the truth in his right eye, as if it were a scrying board, something to be gazed into, seen past. But what she saw, she never shared. Kell took her hand and kissed it. “I’m fine, Your Majesty.” She gave him a weary look, and he corrected himself. “Mother.”</i><br /><br /><i>”I said Rhy forgave them.” Kell pushed to his feet. “I never said I did.”</i><br /><br /><b>Lila Bard:</b><br /><br /><i>”Death comes for everyone,” she said simply. “I’m not afraid of dying. But I am afraid of dying here.” She swept her hand over the room, the tavern, the city. “I’d rather die on an adventure than live standing still.”</i> <br /><br />I’m not entirely sure if I like Lila or not. XD I mean I admire her resilience and stubbornness but I think sometimes she was way too sure of herself and that got her into a lot of trouble. *lol* But oh well, when it comes down to it there is no denying that I actually like her. Her character seems to be somewhat of an acquired taste and I’m curious if she’ll truly become a pirate in the end. Also I could relate to her when it came to her choice of clothes. I would have gone for the boy’s clothes in a heartbeat as well. ;-P (Could it be that Lila is non-binary or gender fluid?!) Generally speaking I think it wasn’t easy to relate to her because she kept everyone at a distance and didn’t let anything get too close to her. For me this made it kind difficult to gauge her character and I hope we’ll get a better grip on it in the next two books. Now that I think about it, I had the same feeling when it came to Blue Sargent throughout the first two books of “The Raven Cycle”. I only really got to know her in “Blue Lily, Lily Blue” so I hope the same will happen with Lila in the next book. XD<br /><br /><i>”What are you?” he asked, amazed.<br />Lila only shrugged. “Stubborn.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Love doesn’t keep us from freezing to death, Kell,” she continued, “or starving, or being knifed for the coins in our pocket. Love doesn’t buy us anything, so be glad for what you have and who you have because you may want for things but you need for nothing.”</i> <br /><br /><b>Holland:</b><br /><br /><i>”He didn’t know if it was the evenness in the man’s tone or his strangely faded appearance or his haunted eyes – one black, of course, the other a milky green. Or perhaps it was the way he seemed to be made more of water and stone than flesh and blood and soul.”</i><br /><br />I love Holland, okay?! I know he’s supposed to be one of the villains but seriously, how could I not adore him?! &lt;3 His character was so multi-layered, complex, calculating, determined and cruel. It was so nice to watch him in action. *lol* I just can’t resist a decent villain and Holland had all the makings of one. XD Especially an intriguing background story. I really wish we would have gotten more of it though. I mean we only got the necessary details to keep the story moving but there are so many things I would have loved to read about. I guess it was Schwab’s intention to keep us in the dark, because this might sound paranoid but I’m <b>CONVINCED</b> that Holland will reappear in the next book! I don’t buy his death!!! There’s no way he died! He said it’s hard to kill an Antari and he was still breathing and alive when Kell sent him to Black London. <u>THE SOURCE</u> of black magic! Hell, this has trouble written all over it! If you ask me Kell basically handed him the means to come back even stronger! &gt;_&lt; Kell is so going to regret this! <br /><br /><i>”Looking into Holland’s eye made her skin crawl. Dark things swirled just beneath the smooth black depths. One word whispered through her mind. Run.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Hesitation is the death of advantage,” mused Holland and Kell fought in vain against the metal pinnings.</i><br /><br /><i>”I hope you made him suffer,” she spat, turning towards the looming castle.<br />No, thought Kell as they set off. He suffered long enough.</i><br /><br /><b>Rhy:</b><br /><br /><i>“Yes. Because unless you plan to wed me yourself – and don’t get me wrong, I think we’d make a dashing pair – I must try and find a mate.”<br />“And you think you’ll find one traipsing around the city?”<br />“Goodness, no,” said Rhy with a crooked grin. “But who knows what fun I’ll find while failing.”</i><br /><br />Rhy is such a precious bean! He gave me Nikolai and Hypnos vibes so it’s no wonder I almost instantly adored him! *lol* He sounds like a lot of fun but unfortunately we didn’t get to see all too much of him in this book. I hope that will change in the next one though. (Also he seems to be unapologetically bi and I live and breathe for characters like that!!!) Still, judging by the little we saw and heard of him I can already tell that he loves Kell like a brother and would never do anything to harm him. I can’t help but wonder what he thinks about his parent’s reaction though. If Kell wouldn’t have been bound to him they would have either killed him or sent him to prison so it’s pretty obvious that Kell was right about their intentions all along. I can’t wait to see more of funny, caring and kind Rhy so there better be more scenes with him in “A Gathering of Shadows”. Also was it just me or did Holland and Rhy actually flirt with each other? It’s such a shame he was merely a means to an end for him. I bet from now on Rhy won’t trust people as easily as before. <br /><br /><i>Rhy’s hands curled into fists. “How could you?” he said, and Kell worried that the prince was bitter about being tethered to him. Instead, Rhy said, “How could you carry that weight?”</i><br /><br /><i>Rhy laughed silently. “I apologize for anything I might have done. I was not myself.”<br />“I apologize for shooting you in the leg,” said Lila. “I was myself entirely.”<br />Rhy broke into his perfect smile.<br />“I like this one,” he said to Kell.</i><br /><br /><b>The Dane Twins:</b><br /><br /><i>”Jealous?” he asked. Holland’s two-toned eyes held Athos’s, the green and the black both steady, unblinking. “He suffered,” added Athos softly. “But not like you.” He brought his mouth closer. “No one suffers as beautifully as you.”</i><br /><br />Okay! Can anyone please tell me how exactly Holland suffered?!!! I mean it’s indicated that there was something sexual and cruel going on between Athos and him but WHAT EXACTLY??!!! Apparently the Dane Twins had a reputation of torturing and forcing people to do their will. And Holland was under their spell as well so I can only assume that he suffered kind of “Rhysand/Amarantha style”? Also there was only a brief mention that Holland didn’t win the throne because he wasn’t cruel enough to take it before the Danes did. What exactly happened before they ascended the White throne?! I really wish we would have gotten more details here, because this really sounded like an interesting story! Either way the Dane twins gave me the creeps. Astrid even more than her brother Athos. Magic and malice indeed. *shudders* They made for pretty intriguing villains for sure. XD I’m just glad Kell never became Astrid’s toy. He certainly wouldn’t have survived it. <br /><br /><i>”Astrid Dane is made of magic and malice.”</i><br /><br /><b>The relationships &amp; ships:</b><br /><br /><u>Lila &amp; Kell:</u><br /><br /><i>”You don’t know anything about these worlds,” he said, but the fight was bleeding out of his voice.<br />“Sure I do,” countered Lila cheerfully. “There’s Dull London, Kell London, Creepy London, and Dead London,” she recited, ticking them off on her fingers. “See? I’m a fast learner.”</i><br /><br />Is it just me or was Kell ending up on Lila’s bed TWICE in one night some sort of a broad hint? The first time it was even BDSM style! *lol* I guess we all know in which direction their future relationship is going to head. Haha! ;-P Also they kissed at least twice for good luck as well and they both had more luck than brain. Right after the motto “Fortune favours fools!” So they didn’t need the luck but obviously were looking for an opportunity to kiss. XD They were very different but for some reason they still worked. Maybe it’s because they balance each other and magic is all about balance as we already learned. Plus they are both Antari. I wonder how their relationship is going to continue. There is a lot of potential that only needs to be explored. ;-P<br /><br /><i>”I’m not going to die,” she said. “Not till I’ve seen it.”<br />“Seen what?”<br />Her smile widened. “Everything.”<br />Kell smiled back. And then Lila brought her free hand to his jaw and tugged his mouth towards hers. The kiss was there and then gone, like one of her smiles.</i><br /><br /><i>A wry smile cut across Lila’s mouth. “You’re a smuggler.”<br />“Says the pickpocket,” snapped Kell defensively.</i><br /><br /><u>Rhy &amp; Kell:</u><br /><br /><i>”What sons our parents have,” said Kell gently. “Between the two of us, we’ll tear the whole world down.”</i> <br /><br />They might not be brothers by blood but they are brothers by heart! &lt;33 I loved their relationship so much and I was so glad that Rhy truly cared about Kell! Which is more than can be said about his parents, but Kell already knew that. &gt;_&lt; I felt so sorry for him but at least he has Rhy and he wouldn’t allow anything to happen to him. Those two seem to balance each other as well and I’m kind of beginning to see a pattern here. *lol* In their relationship dynamic it seems like Rhy is the daredevil who gets into trouble though and Kell is more the mature and responsible one. I can only imagine in which kind of mess they’ll get in the next book. One thing is for sure, I can’t wait to read more about this brotherly duo! ;-P<br /><br /><i>”He looked up and saw me crouching over him, bleeding, and the first thing he said wasn’t ‘What happened?’ or ‘Where are we?’ He touched the blood on his chest and said, ‘Is it yours? Is it all yours?’ and when I nodded, he burst into tears, and I took him home.”</i><br /><br /><b>Conclusion:</b><br /><br />I absolutely LOVED this! <b>“A Darker Shade of Magic”</b> had everything I’m looking for in a book. There was (dark) magic, there were four parallel Londons and there were lots of complex characters I couldn’t help but want to read more about. Yes, the world building and some of the characters themselves might have been rather sketchy, but knowing Schwab I’m certain that we’ll get more details in the following books. This was only just the beginning and what a marvellous one it was! XD<br /><br />___________________________<br /><br />I’m going to read this! <br /><b>FINALLY!!!</b> <br /><br />There are about a thousand of reasons why I wanted to read this for ages and yet I still didn’t manage to get to it! Typical me! <br />I’m going to stop procrastinating now though!<br />I’m ready to tackle this series <u>BECAUSE</u>:<br /><br />- Four parallel Londons! <br />- Magic!<br />- A smuggler!<br />- A thief!<br />- V.E. SCHWAB!!!! <br /><br />Do I even have to say more??!! <br />I’m so ready for this! <br />Just bring it on! I got this! XD</span>
  <a data-text-id="17793063898984120000" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1619565528" />
    <a title="The Burning Rose (Jess)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess"><img alt="The Burning Rose (Jess)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605317941p2/48477217.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1619565528?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Burning Rose (Jess)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Burning Rose (Jess)" href="/user/show/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess">The Burning Rose (Jess)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780765376466" href="/book/show/25667118-a-darker-shade-of-magic">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess?shelf=books-to-own">books-to-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess?shelf=wtb">wtb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1619565528" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2285706140876495035">"Death comes for everyone. I'm not afraid of dying. But I am afraid of dying here. I'd rather die on an adventure than live standing still.”<br/> <br/>And it indeed WAS a great adventure. I’m so glad I picked up this book. Should have done this long ago.<br/> <br/>Kell is a magician named Antari. He has the ability to travel between Londons. Kell works for Red London royalty. Or should I say- was adopted by the royalties. But, he has always felt as a possession and not as a family member. Well, except for the relat</span>
  <span id="freeText2285706140876495035" style="display:none">"Death comes for everyone. I'm not afraid of dying. But I am afraid of dying here. I'd rather die on an adventure than live standing still.”<br /> <br />And it indeed WAS a great adventure. I’m so glad I picked up this book. Should have done this long ago.<br /> <br />Kell is a magician named Antari. He has the ability to travel between Londons. Kell works for Red London royalty. Or should I say- was adopted by the royalties. But, he has always felt as a possession and not as a family member. Well, except for the relationship with Rhy- who he claims to be his brother. <br /><br />There are 4 Londons- Red (Kell’s London), White London (ruled by the Danes), Black London (long gone), and Grey London (which is our London).<br /><br />The setting, the world that Schwab built, is so brilliant and fascinating. The different ways of which London lives, how Kell found names to each London, by the way they function. I especially love the story behind Black London- which is sealed because it was consumed by magic.<br /><br />Kell meets Lila, a pickpocket in grey London- strong and spunky- a girl who desires to be a pirate, and longs for adventure. She finds the opportunity by sticking to Kell’s mission- to return the black stone to Black London- where it belongs.<br /><br />I loved both Kell and Lila, and I really loved how they worked together as a team. I loved the fact that at first they didn’t really care about each other. In fact, the reason they met was because Lila stole the dangerous artifact from Kell. And then- how they found themselves willing to be in a dangerous position just to help each other. There’s no love story- just a great partnership that grows stronger. Which is amazing, because if you know me, you'll know that I appreciate love that comes from acquaintance. And who said there would be romance between them? Even if that seems to happen. And that's the kind of excitement I like- to wait and see what happens between these two.<br /><br />Kell was likable from the very beginning. I love how vulnerable he seemed to be at the beginning, because he wasn’t really in any real danger. Then he realized how strong he really was, and so were we.<br /><br />I also liked Rhy, and I was sad that I didn't get the chance to really know him as a character.<br /><br />Holland is another Antari, who belongs to the dangerous, magic-lusting White London.<br />To be honest, I didn’t like him at first. I knew he was bad only because he couldn’t resist the Danes, and that’s why I understand his motives. But I was angry with him because he tried to kill Kell, and I fucking love Kell. I do hope Holland will be in the sequels because I want to know more about him.<br />Another thing I liked about White London are Athos and Astrid, who were really great villains. They were strong, smart, sadistic and ruthless. It made me excited about the way they behave, and I was curious how Kell would deal with them.<br /><br />The downside that made me give this book only 4 stars is because it wasn’t a book I couldn’t put it down. The beginning was mostly a back story, and it took me a while to get into the vibe of the plot. After the shit started happening- I got hooked (finally) and couldn’t put the book down.<br /><br />By the way- Kell has a mysterious coat that has a different look for every place he visits (and there are so many- some coats he has never seen, or seen once, and then never again). How amazing is that? I want this coat.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2285706140876495035" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
