<div id="review_1868502489" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1868502489" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1868502489?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-high-fantasy">sff-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=genre-experiments">genre-experiments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2017">z-read2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=characters-of-color">characters-of-color</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-series">x-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=mental-illness-disability">mental-illness-disability</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-relationships">favorite-relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-faves2017">z-faves2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1868502489" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8514791185180083418"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I apologize for anything I might have done. I was not myself.”<br/>“I apologize for shooting you in the leg,” said Lila. “I was myself entirely.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><u>
  <b>Actual Rating: 4 1/2 Stars,</b>
</u> but honestly every time I round this down I end up putting it back up a day later. So you may notice this book is kind of polarizing within the adult sff community; a little bit And for me personally it is.... such a fave. I keep returning to this world and these characters and I doubt I’ll ever stop.<br/><br/>For the appro</span>
  <span id="freeText8514791185180083418" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I apologize for anything I might have done. I was not myself.”<br />“I apologize for shooting you in the leg,” said Lila. “I was myself entirely.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><u>
  <b>Actual Rating: 4 1/2 Stars,</b>
</u> but honestly every time I round this down I end up putting it back up a day later. So you may notice this book is kind of polarizing within the adult sff community; a little bit And for me personally it is.... such a fave. I keep returning to this world and these characters and I doubt I’ll ever stop.<br /><br />For the approximately five people who don’t know, <i>A Darker Shade of Magic</i> is about a world with four parallel worlds, all very different but sharing the same London. There’s Grey London, aka our world. Red London, a land of magic and peace. White London, a land of turmoil and war and an overuse of magic. And Black London, the land where magic went wrong and burnt out. Only a few people can travel between worlds, and when one of the only two left, Kell, discovers a magic stone that could destroy his world, he and non-magical Lila go on a journey to put it back. <br /><br />Let's get the problems out of the way - <b>
  <u>the plotting is a mixed bag.</u>
</b> Pro: fast-paced and <b>
  <u>never boring.</u>
</b> This book is a 400-page wild ride. Con: literally <b>
  <u>no driving force</u>
</b> behind the plot. The characters don't even have a quest until around page 200, and it makes the entire book feel just a bit messy. This is a problem Victoria Schwab tends to have a <i>lot</i> [she’s my favorite author so I’m allowed to say this], where her characters just meander around in search of an end goal. This.... kills her series conclusions. Like, it’s killed both of the series enders I’ve read by her for me personally, and this is coming from the bitch who has five starred every single other book I’ve read by her. But it doesn’t really hurt the plot that much here, so it’s fine, and we’ll just address that more in the ACOL review. <br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“What are you?” she asked. <br />“A monster,” said Kell hoarsely. “You'd better let me go.”<br />The girl gave a small, mocking laugh. “Monsters don't faint in the presence of ladies.” <br />“Ladies don't dress like men and pick pockets,” retorted Kell. <br />Her smile only sharpened. “What are you really?” <br />“Tied to your bed," said Kell matter-of-factly.<br />“And?” <br />His brow furrowed. “And in trouble.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />The main thing I always come back to about this book is that it is deeply, deeply <b>
  <u>magical</u>
</b>. It was nigh-impossible for me to <i>not</i> be engaged in this story. The writing style is SO GOOD, lyrical and gorgeous and with a really nice flow to it; one of my good blogger friends discussed her sentence structure, and it is so fantastic. The worldbuilding is creative and intriguing and perhaps best of all, makes a surprising amount of sense for such a wild concept. <br /><br />Also, I would die for these characters. Oddly, they didn't totally grow on me until like... 2/3 of the way into the book? While I could recognize from the beginning that the leads were well-developed and interesting, it took me a while to feel as if I had a concrete concept of who they are. And then we got to the ending and I was screaming in agony at the thought of these characters dying, and I was like "oh shit" and realized how much I love Kell and Lila and Rhy and how much I care about their relationships. V.E. Schwab does a lot of showing, not telling, which makes the character development a bit more subtle; these characters are based off their motivations perhaps even more than their actual traits. And both of these things mean you’re less invested in the beginning and then.... more invested in the end. Slow start, flawless payoff.<br /><br />I actually want to talk a little more specifically about these characters because when I think back on this series, they are <i>always</i> what come to mind. Kell is a grumpy child who we love anyway. Lila is a fucking badass <a href="https://www.tor.com/2017/03/21/ve-schwab-reddit-ama-shades-of-magic-lila-bard-non-binary/" rel="nofollow noopener">genderfluid</a> thief with a soft side and I love her. Rhy is a bisexual prince [literally] who spends half his time dragging people. Even Holland, the sort-of-villain, is a super dynamic and intriguing character. <br /><br />Oh, and then the relationships: Kell and Lila, y’all. Kell and Lila are my ride-or-die book couple and I love their dynamic and I love how they’re constantly dragging each other and just. fuck. I love them. I also really really like Kell and Rhy’s relationship, which is so ridiculously loving and caring? They are perhaps two of the most different people ever and they love each other so much it's beautiful. <br /><br />I also kind of love that 98% of the dynamics in this book kind of read like everyone has dated everyone else and it’s now Really Awkward [this is both Kell &amp; Holland and also Rhy &amp; Holland and it later becomes the canon dynamic of Rhy &amp; Alucard, and it's hilarious]. If anyone wants to come for me about this, I point to <a href="https://twitter.com/veschwab/status/1004008545141043201" rel="nofollow noopener">That Time Victoria Schwab Said That Every Character In This Series Should Be Read As Queer</a>. No, that is not the only reason why I like this series, and yes, they’re all bi icons and you can’t take that away from me. <br /><br />Anyway. Super highly recommended for fans of creative, engaging fantasy. <br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8514791185180083418" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1845323738" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1845323738" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1845323738?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/23403402-a-darker-shade-of-magic">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1845323738" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7496691355509540923"><b>This is an unpopular opinion, if you’re easily offended, please don’t read this review.</b><br/><br/>Okay, 3 stars is still a good rating but I think rating aDSoM 3 stars on Goodreads is like I’m an E.T who arrives in London. This is my sixth month on Goodreads and throughout that period, there are three series that always appeared on my feeds and probably everyone else. First, Six of Crows duology, second, anything that came out of Sarah J Maas’s head and finally, the Shade of Magic trilogy by V.E Schwab. <b>It</b></span>
  <span id="freeText7496691355509540923" style="display:none"><b>This is an unpopular opinion, if you’re easily offended, please don’t read this review.</b><br><br>Okay, 3 stars is still a good rating but I think rating aDSoM 3 stars on Goodreads is like I’m an E.T who arrives in London. This is my sixth month on Goodreads and throughout that period, there are three series that always appeared on my feeds and probably everyone else. First, Six of Crows duology, second, anything that came out of Sarah J Maas’s head and finally, the Shade of Magic trilogy by V.E Schwab. <b>It needed to be said first that I’m not a fan of the YA genre but these series are hyped as drug dealers search for heroin and I decided to give some of them a try with hope it will changed my mind on the genre.</b> Sadly it didn’t, Six of Crows duology disappointed me <i>(Oh look, so many arrows. Casted magic barrier to block all the arrows shooting at me)</i>, this book also disappointed me <i>(Magic Barrier is now broken)</i> and I won’t even touch anything by Sarah J Maas. <i>(Endless arrow pinned me to a wall.)</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1487509214ra/22020893.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Don’t get me wrong, I never said I hated the Six of Crows duology or this book, it disappointed me but I actually think both series is still good to read. I actually liked this book for a while until the underwhelming climax happened. It’s just a shame there are a lot of parts that obstructed me from loving aDSoM. I love V.E Schwab’s work on Vicious, it was unique, morally ambiguous, suited for adult audience and have great characters. It’s why I gave this series a try and turns out I’ve been fooled. aDSoM’s plot is really YA-ish and it’s the exact opposite of what made Vicious great for me.<br><br>There is nothing remotely interesting about the plot. It’s a very typical McGuffin story which had been overdone to death already. These days, there are a lot of stories and themes that have been overdone but somehow managed to deliver immersive and intriguing plot with great casts of characters and their developments. <br><br>That’s the other main problem with ADSoM, I’m so detached from the story and the characters that I honestly don’t care about any of them if they died or not. There are no developments at all for the main characters except Lila. Kell is angsty but he cares about Rhy, Rhy is gay <i>(or bisexual or nymphomania I don’t know, seems like he’ll have sex with anything that moves.)</i> and he cares about Kell, Lila is adventurous, <br><br><b>
  <i>“I'd rather die on an adventure than live standing still.”</i>
</b><br><br>Holland is mysterious and the Dane Twins is sadistic. There, I talked about the main characters personality and their development progression throughout this whole book within one sentence. Lila and Holland is probably the only saving characters of this book, Lila character is more fleshed out compared to the rest and for Holland, he’s just more interesting and every scene where he appears really shine for the book.<br><br><b>Holland and the Dane Twins</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437532514i/15595705._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I honestly prefer Holland to be the main character compared to Kell. Seriously, out of everything I ever read, Kell is one of the most boring character of all time. The only thing intriguing about him is his coat and it's always a bad sign when the clothes is more captivating than the person. Don’t even compare him with Kelsier from Mistborn just because they have similar name, just… don’t.<br><br>Finally, the last problem I have with the book is the underwhelming magic and climax. If there's one thing that V.E Schwab haven't improved since Vicious, it’s definitely the climax scene delivery. Vicious would have received a 5 star from me if it wasn’t for the super underwhelming climax and sadly, it’s still the same here. Even all the action scenes in the book are really standard and provides zero intensity. I read the climax sequences with a face and emotion so flat that drinking a hot Chamomile tea will give more reaction to my emotion.<br><br><b>Now, with all the problems I have with the book, you’re probably wondering why this is not a 1 star or 2 star review. Here’s the thing, even with all the negativity, I still don’t hate the book, I still enjoy reading it. Why? Because of these 3 factors that really shine from aDSoM. 4 alternative London concept, V.E Schwab’s writing and Kell’s Coat, yes that coat is a work of brilliance and deserve an extra star.</b><br><br>The 4 color alternative London is a really great concept, it’s one of the biggest reasons why I bought this book in the first place other than the fact I thought it will be more adult oriented than Vicious. It’s like V.E Schwab took Neil Gaiman’s Neverwhere imagination and gave it a twist to make it her own idea. All 4 version of London have their unique characteristic. <b>Grey London, our version of London which smells like smoke, Red London, Kell’s version of London which smelled like fire, White London, the Dane Twin’s &amp; Holland’s version of London which smelled like blood and finally Black London, the lost London which smelled like teen spirit. Okay I’m joking, there is no known smell to Black London since no one can go there anymore.</b> I do wish there’s an explanation though on why there is 4 London in the first place since the setting is in our real world, maybe the future sequels will enlighten me on this.<br><br>I have always loved Schwab’s writing, her choices of words and pages format never fails to make me turn those pages even when things aren’t interesting. Finally, Kell’s coat, I won’t talk about this much since I honestly think it’s better for you to find out about this peculiar coat on your own. If I have Kell’s coat, I don’t think I’ll ever need another coat again. Take note fashion designers, when you make do a Men’s fashion show, Kell’s Coat is the kind of shit I will buy in a heartbeat.<br><br><b>Not this cereals costume</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487509214i/22020894._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Not this Frankenstein’s monster wannabe, why would I want to eliminate my own neck?</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487509214i/22020895._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>And for the love of all that is holy and sacred not this abomination</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487509214i/22020896._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Despite everything, I still like the book enough to finish it and I still have hope for the future sequels. It won't be soon but I will continue with the series eventually with really low expectation. <b>I’m hoping a Gathering of Shadows and a Conjuring of Light will be better than aDSoM since obviously to me this book is clearly an Overhyped Shade of Magic. It lacked a touch of brilliance to make the book reach its maximum potential that the concept provides and I sincerely hope the sequels will receive the shade of magic it needs.</b><br><br><a href="http://booknest.eu" rel="nofollow noopener">Booknest</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7496691355509540923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1357108272" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4304509243543415051">My spoiler free video review is now up!!: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://youtu.be/hINnk0eqj8I'>https://youtu.be/hINnk0eqj8I</a><br/><br/>4.5 Stars<br/><br/>All I can say is WOW!<br/><br/>That was incredible!! <br/><br/>First off, the characters were FANTASTIC! Schwab is truly a master when it comes to crafting multidimensional, well rounded, and flawed characters. Rhy is so pure and precious. Kell deserves love and happiness. And Lila. Lila Bard is my new queen. <br/><br/>This was truly one of the most realistic fantasy worlds I've ever read about. I mean that in the sense that the world seemed like </span>
  <span id="freeText4304509243543415051" style="display:none">My spoiler free video review is now up!!: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/hINnk0eqj8I">https://youtu.be/hINnk0eqj8I</a><br /><br />4.5 Stars<br /><br />All I can say is WOW!<br /><br />That was incredible!! <br /><br />First off, the characters were FANTASTIC! Schwab is truly a master when it comes to crafting multidimensional, well rounded, and flawed characters. Rhy is so pure and precious. Kell deserves love and happiness. And Lila. Lila Bard is my new queen. <br /><br />This was truly one of the most realistic fantasy worlds I've ever read about. I mean that in the sense that the world seemed like something that could actually exist. The world was complex and intricate, but just grounded enough that the concept of 4 parallel London's is something I can truly conceptualize. In other words, it made me believe that the magic was real. <br /><br />As always, Schwab's writing was absolutely engaging. It's concise and simplistic, yet still full of warmth and depth. This book was a bit slower paced but I thought that it matched the world perfectly. It was fast-paced and action-packed where it needed to be and still took its time to develop the world and characters completely. <br /><br />Needless to say, I loved it. And I can't wait to continue on in the series!</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1291318032" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1291318032" />
    <a title="Cece (ProblemsOfaBookNerd)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5138611-cece-problemsofabooknerd"><img alt="Cece (ProblemsOfaBookNerd)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539540436p2/5138611.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1291318032?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer9621612691064881883">*Upon a reread, my passion for this book stands. I love it so much. I can't believe I actually get to move on to book 2 this time. I JUST LOVE IT. <br/><br/><br/>My thoughts: "Now, think critically. There were one or two things you maybe didn't love quite as much as everything else. A 4.5 accurately sums up your feelings and shows you didn't think the book was absolutely perfect."<br/>My actions: *RUNS DOWN THE STREET SCREAMING "5 STARS OF PERFECTION" AT ANYONE WHO WILL LISTEN*</span>

<div id="review_941896221" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/941896221" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/941896221?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=creeptastic">creeptastic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=the-book-boy-is-mine">the-book-boy-is-mine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=best-of-the-best">best-of-the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=diabolical">diabolical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=that-bastard">that-bastard</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=some-kinda-magic">some-kinda-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=rabid-reads-reviews">rabid-reads-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=cover-whore">cover-whore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=it-burns-us-precious">it-burns-us-precious</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer941896221" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3169760388119191412"><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2015/04/review-a-darker-shade-of-magic-by-v-e-schwab.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>A DARKER SHADE OF MAGIC is one of those books that I needed to reflect upon before reviewing.<br/><br/>As far as I can tell this happens to me for one of two reasons:<br/><br/>1. It was awful, but in a way that confounded me, either b/c it was an author whom I love and trust and WTH happened? Or b/c my issue(s) is nebulous and thus has to be dissected to determine the root of the problem.<br/>2. It was amazeballs, but in a way that confounded me, b/c SO MUCH CLEVER. <br/><br/>This was a #2 situati</span>
  <span id="freeText3169760388119191412" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2015/04/review-a-darker-shade-of-magic-by-v-e-schwab.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br><b>4.5 stars</b><br><br>A DARKER SHADE OF MAGIC is one of those books that I needed to reflect upon before reviewing.<br><br>As far as I can tell this happens to me for one of two reasons:<br><br>1. It was awful, but in a way that confounded me, either b/c it was an author whom I love and trust and WTH happened? Or b/c my issue(s) is nebulous and thus has to be dissected to determine the root of the problem.<br>2. It was amazeballs, but in a way that confounded me, b/c SO MUCH CLEVER. <br><br>This was a #2 situation. Fyi.<br><br>And even though it's been over a month, I'm still kind of at odds about what to say.<br><br>Firstly, it is a fact universally acknowledged that I am a character-driven reader.<br><br>BUT.<br><br>I was not more than mildly invested in these characters until I was more than halfway through it.<br><br>Secondly, it is a fact universally acknowledged that ROMANCE, I love it.<br><br>Yet there was very little romance in this book.<br><br>SO. We have:<br><br>1. Characters I didn't immediately connect with. <br>2. Little to no swoons.<br><br>And still . . . I LOVED it.<br><br>Do you see why I needed time to traverse the dark and twisty paths of my mind? But ultimately, it comes down to this:<br><br>Victoria Schwab is a bloodydamn genius.<br><br>No really. She is. <br><br>She created a world so vastly different from others I've encountered, with hinted at conundrums for a later date, and characters who are . . . oblivious yet discerning, adventurous and daring, scared but determined, arrogant yet realistic, but above all else they are <em>compelling</em>. They are also broken. In remarkably similar ways despite the disparity of their situations.<br><br>Kell is a member of the royal family. A prince. Brother to the heir. <br><br>Except he isn't. And he knows it, they know it, <em>everyone</em> knows it. B/c Kell . . . is a young man with a rare and remarkable ability, and was therefore removed whence he came to become an adjunct extension of a pre-existing family.<br><br>But everyone pretends.<br><br>Just like Kell pretends not to be consumed with questions about what came <em>before</em>. <br><br>Lila . . . *shakes head at Lila* <br><br>Lila is a young woman who refuses to be confined by the restrictions of both her gender and her station. She is astonishingly intelligent. She is independent. If she had a middle name, it would almost certainly be Hubris. <br><br>And yet, she is bitterly fragile. <br><br>She wants nothing from no one, and accepts nothing she cannot immediately repay, negating any debt she feels is owed. <br><br>She's painful to watch. <br><br>But I had to watch. Had to. If for no other reason, then to see what she would say/think next:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>The rich strutted around, assuming they'd be safe, so long as they stayed in the good parts of town. But Lila knew there were no good parts. Only smart parts and stupid parts, and she was quick enough to know which one to play.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>DO YOU SEE WHAT SHE DID THERE?! *head explodes b/c can't contain the awesome*<br><br>That kind of brilliance is around every corner. That kind of brilliance is why, for the first time ever, I neither DNF-ed a book b/c characters I didn't connect with or lamented my decision to stick with it after the fact. And honestly, I have no idea what my problem was. I've already said that, yes, eventually, they began to tug my heartstrings, but why it took so long . . . ? It shall remain a mystery.<br><br>But things like this:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I'm not going to die," she said. "Not till I've seen it."<br>"Seen what?"<br>Her smile widened. "Everything."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>were the turning point.<br><br>Plot-wise, I'm not going to say anything, b/c the less you know, the better. <br><br>As for world-building, take the things you think you know about magic systems and toss them out the window.<br><br>When I first learned that one of the rulers of Red London had a special talent for controlling the will of others, I was like, "Well, that sucks," and when Kell walked up the fortress steps that were guarded by ten soldiers who were indeed controlled, I thought, "That is <em>such</em> a waste of power. How many people could this guy possibly control at once, and how could he have any power left over to defend against a direct magical attack?"<br><br>But I had made an incorrect assumption. Just b/c that's the way magic typically works, doesn't mean that's the way it works according to Schwab. <br><br>Arthos can control <em>as many people as he wants</em>. All he has to do is brand them with his particular kind of magic. And that, my friends, is terrifying. <br><br> And all of that is why A DARKER SHADE OF MAGIC will be near the top of my Best Books of 2015 list. You will laugh at drunk men stumbling groggily on stairs (HA!), you will nod your head thoughtfully as Kell and Lila reveal the intricacies of what makes them tick, you will gasp in shock and horror when you find yourself walking across the bones of defeated enemies, and you will not regret reading this book for yourself. Highly recommended.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>My other reviews for this series:</b><br><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1218954728" rel="nofollow noopener">A Gathering of Shadows (Shades of Magic, #2)</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1510375081" rel="nofollow noopener">A Conjuring of Light (Shades of Magic, #3)</a>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="3169760388119191412" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765399113" href="/book/show/34496775-a-darker-shade-of-magic">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1672517370" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13610554498167174520"><b>I read this again. I really don’t know if I want it to be a three star; maybe lower. I’m seriously changing how I feel over books or maybe I really felt that way. I just know I’m unhauling many things. I am going to keep the audibles of these books as I do like the narration</b><br/><br/>**************************************<br/><br/>This is the first book I have read by this author and it won't be the last. I thought this one was pretty good. I didn't even think I would like it at first and I'm not sure why, but I di</span>
  <span id="freeText13610554498167174520" style="display:none"><b>I read this again. I really don’t know if I want it to be a three star; maybe lower. I’m seriously changing how I feel over books or maybe I really felt that way. I just know I’m unhauling many things. I am going to keep the audibles of these books as I do like the narration</b><br><br>**************************************<br><br>This is the first book I have read by this author and it won't be the last. I thought this one was pretty good. I didn't even think I would like it at first and I'm not sure why, but I did. There were some parts that got on my nerves here and there but that's the way that goes right?<br><br>The idea of Kell being able to walk into different parts of London was totally cool! You have Grey, Red, White and Black &lt;----but no one goes to black for reasons I will not name. <br><br>They have some nutzy cuckoo people in White London. A king and queen that are evil incarnate. <br><br>Kell goes around and takes messages to other parts of London. He lives in the Red part with the royal family there. But I'm telling you if someone asked me to take a message to the white part, I would tell them to stick it up their arse! Read the book and you will understand. I like Kell's character, he's really nice. He has one black eye though and that would be freak me out just a wee bit at first. Kell also smuggles things for people and collects some cool things. He's a cool magician that travels to these parallel worlds that I find so bizarre and cool at the same time. Well, okay not to the White London... just no! <br><br>Some things go down and Kell ends up in Grey London and he meets Lila Bard. I love Lila! She is a pickpocket and pretty much lives her life that way. But she secretly wants to be a pirate and have her own ship! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466357850i/19471963._SY540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Lila and Kell becomes friends after a little bit of arguing and what not. I think they are cool together and Lila is very fierce for a human =)<br><br><b>EXCERPTS<br><br>Lila Bard lived by a simple rule: if a thing was worth having, it was worth taking. <br><br>She held the silver pocket watch up to the faint glow of the streetlamp, admiring the metal's polished shine, wondering what the engraved initials--L.L.E--on the back might stand for. She'd nicked the watch off a gentleman, a clumsy collision on a too-crowded curb that had led to a swift apology, a hand on a shoulder to distract from a hand on the coat. Lila's fingers weren't just fast; they were light. A tip of the top hat and a pleasant good night, and she was the proud new owner of a timepiece, and he was on his way and none the wiser. <br><br>••••••••••••••<br><br>"Lila," said Kell gently. "I'm sorry."<br>Her fingers curled tightly around the timepiece as she rose to her feet. Kell rose with her, and even though she would not look him in the eye, he could see the anger and pain written in the lines of her face. <br>"When it's over," she said, tucking the watch into a fold of her cloak. "I want to be the one to slit his throat." And then she straightened and let out a small, shuddering breath. "Now," she said. "which way to Fletcher?"</b><br><br>I really wonder what is in store in the next book because of the way it ended. <br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/06/a-darker-shade-of-magic-by-v-e-schwab.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

<div id="review_1920506835" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1920506835" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1920506835?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765399113" href="/book/show/34496775-a-darker-shade-of-magic">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=otp">otp</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-ebooks">owned-ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=the-best-of-the-best">the-best-of-the-best</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1920506835" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5810770323863125261"><blockquote>#1 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1920506835' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Darker Shade of Magic</a> ★★★★★ <br/>#2 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1971365618' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Gathering of Shadows</a> ★★★★★<br/>#3 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2122460535' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Conjuring of Light</a> ★★★★★</blockquote><br/><b>"There's Dull London, Kell London, Creepy London, and Dead London. See? I'm a fast learner."</b> <br/><br/><i>Despite the fact that the four Londons share a name, they have little else in common; one is brimming with life, one is held captive by wicked rulers, one has no magic at all, and one is dead. While there used to be traversing between the Londons, now the doors have been sealed to all except the </i>Antari<i>: magicians</i></span>
  <span id="freeText5810770323863125261" style="display:none"><blockquote>#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1920506835" rel="nofollow noopener">A Darker Shade of Magic</a> ★★★★★ <br>#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1971365618" rel="nofollow noopener">A Gathering of Shadows</a> ★★★★★<br>#3 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2122460535" rel="nofollow noopener">A Conjuring of Light</a> ★★★★★</blockquote><br><b>"There's Dull London, Kell London, Creepy London, and Dead London. See? I'm a fast learner."</b> <br><br><i>Despite the fact that the four Londons share a name, they have little else in common; one is brimming with life, one is held captive by wicked rulers, one has no magic at all, and one is dead. While there used to be traversing between the Londons, now the doors have been sealed to all except the </i>Antari<i>: magicians with the ability to command blood itself, allowing them to travel between the parallels.<br><br>One of the last two remaining </i>Antari<i> in the world, Kell, is the unofficial carrier of messages between the three living Londons, but his entire world comes crumbling down around him when he is tricked into taking a magical object that has enemies hunting him down from one city to the next. When Lila, a young thief and aspiring pirate, is drawn into the middle of his adventure, Kell must learn that the boundaries between good and evil magic aren't as defined as he once thought they were, and he must straddles those boundaries to right what has been made wrong.</i><br><br>---<br><br>This book was my first ever Schwab read, and I went into it a little bit apprehensive, because she is so widely loved that I wondered if this series would live up to the expectations I had for it. I picked it up for the <a href="https://www.facebook.com/groups/688477338003037/" rel="nofollow noopener">Life &amp; Lit</a> June group read, and ended up putting it off until the last possible minute because I was so wary, but my nervousness was entirely unfounded. This book was phenomenal!<br><br><b>KELL ➳➳</b><br>What can I even say? Kell is one of the most lovable male MCs I've seen in a <i>really</i> long time. He's so loving and protective, despite his ongoing self-identity crises regarding his family. He loves his brother Rhy with a fierceness that I couldn't get enough of, and he's just so genuinely <i>good</i> in his heart that I couldn't help but root for him. He's one of those MCs that makes me afraid to continue the series because I can't handle anything terrible happening to him.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499053192ra/23185640.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>LILA ➳➳</b><br>I didn't really know what to make of Lila at first, because to be frank, her excuses for thievery kind of rubbed me the wrong way. Like... you're just going to steal from all of these people because you can? I wouldn't have minded so much if she just stole food or whatever, but trinkets? (I revisited this annoyance a few times later in the book, too.) Overall, though, I really enjoyed her sassy attitude and the way she refused to let anyone tell her what to do or hold her down. I loved that she insisted on going on an adventure, even if it meant risking her life, and her interactions with Kell were just adorable.<br><br><b>RHY ➳➳</b><br>Adorable. Absolutely adorable. He actually made me cry a few times because he just is so pure and innocent and golden.<br><br><b>HOLLAND ➳➳</b><br>Holland honestly gave me <i>the</i> sketchiest vibes ever from the beginning, but I think he's a fantastic character and I pitied him more often than not. I know some shit went down, but I really hope we get to learn more about him later in the series.<br><br><b>PLOT &amp; WORLD ➳➳</b><br>I thought the plot, as well as the world-building, were absolutely incredible. I loved the idea of these parallel cities that the <i>Antari</i> could travel between, and I thought the magic system was beautifully built up. Too many books ignore the foundation for their magic systems and you're kind of left just going, "oh, well, it's magic and that's that," but Schwab didn't do that at all in this book. The idea of these <i>Antari</i> being sort of the chosen ones who could control blood was just badass as hell, and I really hope that Kell and Holland aren't actually the only ones left.<br><br><b>WRITING ➳➳</b><br>Like I said, this was my first time ever reading anything by Victoria Schwab, so I had no idea what to expect. My very first impression from the opening segment,<br><br><i>
  <blockquote>Kell wore a very peculiar coat.<br><br>It had neither one side, which would be conventional, nor two, which would be unexpected, but several, which was, of course, impossible.</blockquote>
</i><br><br>was that her writing reminded me a great deal of Tolkien, circa <i>The Hobbit</i>. As I got further into the book, I did find that Victoria's voice is very much her own, but I enjoyed it to no end. It was the perfect balance of straightforward and flowery prose, and it painted a splendid picture while never wasting too much time on the details.<br><br><b>FINAL VERDICT ➳➳</b><br>Overall, I thought this book was a fantastic beginning to a series and I cannot wait to continue with book #2. I gave this an easy 5/5 stars and would recommend it to anyone who likes three-dimensional high fantasy read, full of a delightful set of characters and a terrifically intriguing world.<br><br>You can find this review (and more) on my blog <a href="https://howlinglibraries.com/2017/07/06/085/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5810770323863125261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2478890431201866830"><i>“A life worth having is a life worth taking.”</i><br/><br/>Wow. I'm stunned and I'm in awe.<br/><br/>Incredible world-building, beautiful language and an intruiging plot make this 5 out of 5 stars.   <span id="freeText2478890431201866830" style="display:none"><i>“A life worth having is a life worth taking.”</i><br /><br />Wow. I'm stunned and I'm in awe.<br /><br />Incredible world-building, beautiful language and an intruiging plot make this 5 out of 5 stars. And let's not forget about the "cross-dressing thieves", "sadistics kings (and queens)" and my favourite the "royal who is equal parts Prince Harry and Jack Harkness". I love Rhy.<br /><br />This novel started as it ended: magical, sensational and breath-taking. It is as beautiful from the outside, as it is from the inside. It's the kind of book you want to keep reading and at the same time to never end.<br /><br />This is one of the best examples of world-building there is. A world (or better: four worlds) so complex and so big, needs a skilled writer to make it feel real. Schwab mastered that skill and made ADSOM far from one-dimensional. There is so much to see, so much to feel, so much to find out. A book like this keeps you pondering for quite a while and even longer.<br /><br />Victoria Schwab turns out to be one of my new favorite authors.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18356045990605012151">*Major spoilers ahead. They won’t be marked*<br/><br/>I was really hesitant going into this one because hello??? I usually end up hating on the most hyped books loved by all my friends. However, I’m so fucking happy and shocked that I <i>actually</i> enjoyed this. <br/><br/>This book is dark and gripping book full of magic. I loved it and I wanted to give this 5 stars, I really wanted to, but the beginning took some time getting into and it was very dull and boring. The beginning of this book felt like I was reading a tex</span>
  <span id="freeText18356045990605012151" style="display:none">*Major spoilers ahead. They won’t be marked*<br /><br />I was really hesitant going into this one because hello??? I usually end up hating on the most hyped books loved by all my friends. However, I’m so fucking happy and shocked that I <i>actually</i> enjoyed this. <br /><br />This book is dark and gripping book full of magic. I loved it and I wanted to give this 5 stars, I really wanted to, but the beginning took some time getting into and it was very dull and boring. The beginning of this book felt like I was reading a textbook. The writing was bland and there was lots of info dump towards the beginning. Later on, I did grasp the idea of the different Londons and magic. This book has such a fantastic world building and once the info dump was over, I understood it all. Anyways, the book did get better, <i>a lot better</i> when <b>Lila Bard</b> made an appearance. Things got 200% more fun and interesting and I WAS HOOKED. <br /><br />●This is a reaaaaaaal slow burner and guess what? I loved it. I seriously fucking hate slow plots, but this book does it so well, it’s impossible not to like it?? This book is literally almost perfection from multiple Londons, complex sexy coats (yes I have issues), badassery, badass female leads, RHY (my new husband, guys), KELL, magic, and evil. The plot of this book seems like any other plot with evil magic on the loose and then we have a hero who has to save the world from bad people *cough* FUCKING HOLLAND AND THE FUCK FACE DANE TWINS* who want to misuse the magic, but Schwab has a way of weaving this plot into something entirely new and thrilling once more for me. It seems so original and gripping even though I’ve a hundred other books with such a similar plot. <br /><br />●I love how this book had no romance AT ALL (well maybe a little). Yo guys, it’s <b>refreshing</b> to read a book where the characters don’t think about kissing and fucking each other while trying to save the world. I like books with a <i>litttttlllleeeee</i> bit of well done romance so I was kind of worried this book would turn out dull because I’ve heard there was no romance, but WORRY NOT, it was bloody fantastic. I couldn’t stop myself from shipping Kell and Lila. However, I’m actually really glad they had no romantic development because Kell and Lila staying just as friends (??) is much much better and refreshing. <s>I WANT LILA AND KELL TO HAVE SOME SWEATY SEX OKAY BYE</s>.<br /><br />-This book has a captivating plot, characters that will make your heart ache and villains that you'll want to fucking murder so bad. Overall, IT HAS LITERALLY EVERYTHING YOU CAN WISH FOR, SO GO FUCKING READ IT OKAY.<br /><br />Another thing that made this book much much more enjoyable for me was turning innocent quotes into dirty quotes. :)) <br />*Lmao just check these status updates out for all the dirty*<br />-<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user_status/show/130686944">https://www.goodreads.com/user_status...</a><br />-<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user_status/show/130617894">https://www.goodreads.com/user_status...</a><br />-<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user_status/show/130564053">https://www.goodreads.com/user_status...</a><br />-<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user_status/show/130476440">https://www.goodreads.com/user_status...</a><br /><br />Other than that guys, I want to marry Rhy bc he’s such a flirty, sweet bastard, how can anyone not love him??? I want to adopt Kell as my new son and go cut some bitches with Lila Bard. Oh, I would particulary like to cut that Holland bitch right in the face, that would be great! :) LMAO SORRY I HATE HIM, WHY DO PEOPLE LOVE HIM???<br /><br /><br />****<br />oh my fucking balls of titanium, my soul is hurting, who the fuck allowed this ???<br /><br />i love Kell and Lila Bard the bitch so so much i love these characters. <br /><br />full rtc soon</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1766354609?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="sreeja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="sreeja" href="/user/show/50309540-sreeja">sreeja</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1766354609" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10711550797323458399">I don’t know what I can say that hasn’t been said before. But in short, this is just perfect. Every page is magic and every scene has a purpose. The characters bring life into this book. The magic system and the writing style is unique and a breath of fresh air. VE Schwab’s writing style truly shines through and I loved every moment of this. Reading this book feels like stumbling into something wholly new and familiar at the same time. Reading this was an adventure with magic and drama. Reading </span>
  <span id="freeText10711550797323458399" style="display:none">I don’t know what I can say that hasn’t been said before. But in short, this is just perfect. Every page is magic and every scene has a purpose. The characters bring life into this book. The magic system and the writing style is unique and a breath of fresh air. VE Schwab’s writing style truly shines through and I loved every moment of this. Reading this book feels like stumbling into something wholly new and familiar at the same time. Reading this was an adventure with magic and drama. Reading this felt like taking on this world, (and other worlds), it was such an amazing experience.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10711550797323458399" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5580268154618457372">i have an unexpected three day weekend and i cant think of a more productive way to spend it than by starting a new series/trilogy! so i did queen schwab the honour of entering and experiencing her world of many londons.<br/><br/>okay, one thing that i have come to realise is that schwab is a grower, not a shower, as it takes me quite some time before i feel settled within her stories. i would even say she has perfected the art of a slow burn because at times when i didnt feel like anything is happening, </span>
  <span id="freeText5580268154618457372" style="display:none">i have an unexpected three day weekend and i cant think of a more productive way to spend it than by starting a new series/trilogy! so i did queen schwab the honour of entering and experiencing her world of many londons.<br /><br />okay, one thing that i have come to realise is that schwab is a grower, not a shower, as it takes me quite some time before i feel settled within her stories. i would even say she has perfected the art of a slow burn because at times when i didnt feel like anything is happening, i was still enjoying myself. and im certain that had to do with the brilliant writing and world building. im very much a plot person, so i was thrilled when i found myself not caring about what was going to happen next because i was so caught up with the characters and the environment and the magic. the writing was so detailed and skilled, and i think that made all the difference for me. <br /><br />overall, this was an very entertaining read! even though most of the time i had no idea where the story/series was going (and i still dont because this could have worked as a standalone), i would be lying if i said i wasnt desperate to find out. so bring on book two!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4 stars</i></b></span>

</a><br/><br/>So... <br/>I finally finished this book. I say finally because it took me a lot to get through - and into- it, and I'm not entirely satisfied with what I read.<br/>I'm a huge Victoria Schwab's fan, she's both an amazing author and a really kind person that I'd spend days worshiping. Vicious is one of my favorite books of all time and her writing is very original. <br/>Yet this book...<br/><a href='https://gifyu.com/image/pFIV' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1513980832ra/24740352.gif' alt='Let_me_think_uhm_um_eh_ooh_yuck_dunno_weird_crazy_britney_huh_what_damn_creepy_icky_whoop_nah.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>I can't tell you if I loved it or not, if maybe I should try and reread it in another moment, because maybe I'm too dumb</span>
  <span id="freeText11545223416419185404" style="display:none"><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/dXXz" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>So... <br>I finally finished this book. I say finally because it took me a lot to get through - and into- it, and I'm not entirely satisfied with what I read.<br>I'm a huge Victoria Schwab's fan, she's both an amazing author and a really kind person that I'd spend days worshiping. Vicious is one of my favorite books of all time and her writing is very original. <br>Yet this book...<br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/pFIV" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1513980832ra/24740352.gif" alt="Let_me_think_uhm_um_eh_ooh_yuck_dunno_weird_crazy_britney_huh_what_damn_creepy_icky_whoop_nah.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

Not here, not there. In the middle. <br>It's not a bad book -quite the opposite, actually-, and I do get the hype to some extent, but maybe I wished that it suit my reader needs more than it actually does. <br>The magic system is probably the thing I liked the most, it added that dark atmosphere I always expect in one of VS's books. <br>I can't say the same for the characters, unfortunately, because, aside from Rhy - and sometimes Kell, too- I didn't like any character in particular. I'm looking at you, Lila. You were a pain. <br>The plot is good, I love London and the way its portrayed, but I had trouble following the writing at times. I found some parts a little dull or anticlimactic, and I had to put it down often because I kept getting distracted by other things. <br>The twists and stabs were absolutely great, though. I can see a lot of her writing in dynamic scenes and I appreciate the author's talent. <br>Overall, this is a good book, and I'm probably going to continue with the trilogy when I have some time. <br>I just feel like something is missing.<br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/pRBK" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_1182211403" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1182211403" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1182211403?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=adventure-like-stuff">adventure-like-stuff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=magic-stuff">magic-stuff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1182211403" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12233582860295295766">3.5 stars<br/><br/>There was just something about this one that kept it from totally rocking, and I can't quite put my finger on what it was. It was<i> good</i>, just not (for me) <i>great</i>.<br/>Kinda dry maybe? Or I just didn't totally connect with the characters? <br/>Not sure.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444667330ra/16533446.gif' width='400' height='220' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>But it's still one of those books that I'm glad I read, and I'm actually <i>really</i> looking forward to reading more about this world/worlds that Schwab created. <br/>And I seriously mean that! There's something cool about this setting and these characters that</span>
  <span id="freeText12233582860295295766" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br><br>There was just something about this one that kept it from totally rocking, and I can't quite put my finger on what it was. It was<i> good</i>, just not (for me) <i>great</i>.<br>Kinda dry maybe? Or I just didn't totally connect with the characters? <br>Not sure.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444667330ra/16533446.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But it's still one of those books that I'm glad I read, and I'm actually <i>really</i> looking forward to reading more about this world/worlds that Schwab created. <br>And I seriously mean that! There's something cool about this setting and these characters that makes me want to see what's going to happen next. I kind of feel like maybe the first book was just a set-up, and now that the world-building is done, this series (trilogy?) is gonna take off!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444667330ra/16533447.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Because that happens, right? Book one is sorta dry and crunchy, and then book two rocks!<br><i>*nods head*</i><br>Yes. I'm feeling confident about that prediction for some reason. I loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/729148703" rel="nofollow noopener">Vicious</a>, I loved the world that she created in this one...totally confident.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444667330ra/16533448.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>*cough*</i><br>Anyway. My point is that I can see why so many of my friends loved this, and I don't want anyone to mistake a 3.5 rating as something bad.<br><i>I don't understand why anyone would think that to start with, but...there's always one.<br>*eyeballs crowd*</i><br>So the gist of the story is that this wizard<i>ish</i> (Traveler) character named Kell is one of the 2 people alive who has the ability to move between worlds. <i>
  <b>Londons</b>
</i>, to be exact. <br>There are 4 different alternate worlds out there, and the only thing they have in common is that London is a city in each of them. <br><b>Grey London = Us </b><br>There's no magic left in our world.<br><b>Red London = Kell</b><br>His world has a perfect balance with magic, and it's a pretty nice place to live.<br><b>White London = Dangerous</b> <br>Their world has squeezed magic so hard that it's retreating from them. It's filled with desperate people willing to do bad shit for power.<br><b>Black London = Dead</b><br>Something happened and they were overtaken by evil magic, sealed off from the other worlds, and now exists only as a cautionary tale.<br><i>The point?</i><b> Magic is real!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444667330ra/16533449.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Without spoiling anything, he gets robbed by a scrappy thief from our Grey London, and the two form a strange friendship/partnership. It's sweet without being romantic...YET. And that's a real selling point for me. It's not that I don't lovelovelove romance in my books, but as I get older/more crotchety, I find myself seriously digging the <b>Slow Burn</b> storylines better than the instant attraction stuff. I get the appeal, but it just makes me scoff at this point in my life. When I read about a couple who seem to fly into each other's arms in a fit of passion, all while declaring their undying love for each other? Instead of oohing and cooing like a normal person...<br><b>This! This is what I see!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444667330ra/16533450.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok, besides a non-awkward romance, this has a few other cool things going for it, as well.<br><b>1)</b> Cool family dynamics! Kell's part of a magical Royal Family. Well, <i>sorta</i>, but not really. It's...<i>complicated</i>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444667330ra/16533451.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>2)</b> Delilah (possibly) has a secret origin! Is there more to her than meets the <b>eye</b>? <i>*wink, wink*</i> <br><b>{insert spoilery inside joke here}</b><br>Still, even without anything extra, she's a tough little cookie. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444667330ra/16533452.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>3)</b> The worlds themselves are just plain interesting. I think Schwab did a good job describing the different Londons because all of them felt very real and well thought out. But I've always had a thing for alternate versions of our world stacked on top of each other, so this was right up my ally, to begin with! And how cool would it be to have the ability to slide in and out of each of those?!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444667330ra/16533453.gif" width="360" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok, so even if it didn't really satisfy me as much as I had hoped, I'm all in for the next book!<br><br>Also reviewed for: <br><div>
  <a href="http://www.addicted2heroines.com/2015/11/review-darker-shade-of-magic-darker.html" title="Addicted 2 Heroines" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412937777i/11444542.jpg" alt="Addicted 2 Heroines" width="100%" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div></span>

<div id="review_2103166400" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2103166400" />
    <a title="Robin Hobb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17730703-robin-hobb"><img alt="Robin Hobb" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442450400p2/17730703.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2103166400?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin Hobb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin Hobb" href="/user/show/17730703-robin-hobb">Robin Hobb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2103166400" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11890099620516890423">I recently met V.E. Schwab and found her entertaining and charming. So I acquired one of her books! I don't think my review of this work is affected by knowing the author, but I like to be transparent.<br/><br/>I always like to avoid spoilers, but in this case, I think the book jacket gives away a bit of the setting, so I'll share it here as well. Imagine four Londons, existing simultaneously but separately. Each has a differing amount of magic, with black London a loss, and Red London a place where magic</span>
  <span id="freeText11890099620516890423" style="display:none">I recently met V.E. Schwab and found her entertaining and charming. So I acquired one of her books! I don't think my review of this work is affected by knowing the author, but I like to be transparent.<br /><br />I always like to avoid spoilers, but in this case, I think the book jacket gives away a bit of the setting, so I'll share it here as well. Imagine four Londons, existing simultaneously but separately. Each has a differing amount of magic, with black London a loss, and Red London a place where magic is like an extra sensory level. Kell is our protagonist, a young man with the very rare ability to travel among the London's. Indeed, that is one of his duties, for the royalty of each London are aware of one another and wish to stay in touch. Kell is a de facto member of the royal family of Red London, treated as a son and brother, but also as a value possession.The one thing that is forbidden to Kell is to bring artifacts or souvenirs from one London to another. <br /><br />And of course, that is the pivot point of the story. And it should be enough to intrigue you into sampling it.<br /><br />The tale is told from multiple points of view. I liked how the characters were introduced as well as how the Londons were shown. No time is wasted in pulling the reader into the story, and once the action begins, it is relentless. I was pleased to see how advanced magic mimics technology in Red London, for I feel that this is an aspect that is often neglected in stories of worlds where magic exists and is exploited as commonplace. I also felt that the way Kell is exploited by his adoptive and loving family has deep roots in human nature. Given the ruthless nature of Kell's antagonists, the story does not flinch from some very dark violence. All good points in my estimation.<br /><br />Quibbles: This book is part of a longer series. As I drew toward the close and realized that not all the conflicts could be resolved in the remaining number of pages, I wished that I had known that from the start. At one point in the story, the characters have a sanctuary and an ally that I wished had been introduced sooner. But both of these quibbles are based on my personal preference and may not impact your reading enjoyment at all! And given the teaser chapter in the back of this book, it looks as if A Gathering of Shadows may focus more on one of the characters I especially enjoyed.<br /><br />All in all, a solidly constructed fantasy with fully realized characters and a unique setting!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11890099620516890423" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1532011218" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1532011218" />
    <a title="Nat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23381142-nat"><img alt="Nat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588309995p2/23381142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1532011218?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nat" href="/user/show/23381142-nat">Nat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23381142-nat?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1532011218" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5102023982612614507"><i>Magic was a living thing—that, everyone knew—but to Kell it felt like more, like a friend, like family. It was, after all, a part of him (much more than it was a part of most) and he couldn’t help feeling like it knew what he was saying, what he was feeling, not only when he summoned it, but always, in every heartbeat and every breath. He was, after all, <b>Antari.</b></i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445955450ra/16725617.gif' width='340' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/>*This review contains <b>spoilers</b>.*<br/><br/>I just finished this book and my mind is all over the place. <br/>I went into this book not knowing much abo</span>
  <span id="freeText5102023982612614507" style="display:none"><i>Magic was a living thing—that, everyone knew—but to Kell it felt like more, like a friend, like family. It was, after all, a part of him (much more than it was a part of most) and he couldn’t help feeling like it knew what he was saying, what he was feeling, not only when he summoned it, but always, in every heartbeat and every breath. He was, after all, <b>Antari.</b></i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445955450ra/16725617.gif" width="340" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>*This review contains <b>spoilers</b>.*<br><br>I just finished this book and my mind is all over the place. <br>I went into this book not knowing much about the plot except that it involved magic and that everyone seemed to love it. <br><br>A lot happened in this book, I’m not even sure where to begin. <br><b>A Darker Shade of Magic</b> has amazingly complex characters (among my favorites: Prince Rhy, Lila Bard, and of course <i>Kell</i>) they made it impossible to put the book down. <br>This book was so original and creative. I had to stop everything I was doing and just finish it.<br>V.E Schwab's writing is outstanding.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1403886368ra/10158219.gif" width="350" height="210" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Kell’s relationship with his brother was incredibly heartwarming. I love close families in YA books. <br><br><i>“Would you tell them?” asked Kell.<br>Rhy sighed. Kell watched him try to answer several ways before he finally said, “There is nothing I would not give you.”<br>Kell’s chest ached. “I know.”<br>“You are my brother. My closest friend.”<br>“I know.”</i><br><br>Also, can we talk about Holland? <br>When we first met Holland I thought he was going to be on Kell’s side. It seemed (to me) that underneath all the evil and pain that had gotten into his body, there was still a flicker of humanity. Unfortunately, I was wrong. <br>I’m kind of sad that he didn’t turn out to be like I originally thought- and watching him suffer at the hands of the Dane twins was extremely painful. I felt extremely relieved when Lila and Kell killed both of the twins. <br><br><i>“Holland knew. He’d seen the attack coming, and he hadn’t stopped it. The instant before the metal struck him from behind, Holland had stopped fighting. It was only a second, a fraction of a breath, but it had been enough to give Kell the edge, the opening. And in the sliver of time after the metal pierced his body, and before he fell, it wasn’t anger or pain that crossed his face. It was relief.”</i><br>I’m glad Holland got his peace.<br><br><br>I also loved loved loved reading from Lila’s point of view. I was anticipating the two main characters meeting right from the start- and it did not disappoint. The chemistry between Lila and Kell felt so real.<br><br><i>“How did you know?” she asked, looking down at the rubble of the queen. “How did you know she wasn’t me?”<br>Kell managed an exhausted smile. “Because she said <b>please.</b>”<br>Lila stared at him, aghast. “Is that a joke?”<br>Kell shrugged slightly. It took a lot of effort. “I just knew,” he said.<br>“You just knew,” she echoed.”</i><br><br>Need the next book now.<br><br>Oh, and this <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KrT_0J6m6y8" rel="nofollow noopener">song</a> made my reading experience 10 times better (I’m still listening to it on repeat).<br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">This review and more can be found on my blog.</a></span>
